**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. **1.2: Administration's Handling of Case Files and Investigations**

**DAILY INTELLIGENCE BRIEFING: JULY 2025**
**FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**

**Area 1: The Jeffrey Epstein Scandal: Political & Legal Fallout**

**1.1: The Wall Street Journal Report and Trump Lawsuit**
The dominant political crisis of the day revolves around President Trump's aggressive response to media reporting on his past association with Jeffrey Epstein. The President has filed a $10 billion libel lawsuit against Dow Jones, the publisher of the Wall Street Journal, in direct response to an article concerning their past relationship [1, 2]. The lawsuit specifically targets a report on allegedly "bawdy" birthday letters the President sent to Epstein, a story that has forced the White House onto the defensive [3]. This legal challenge is being interpreted in two ways: as a personal action by the President and, by some observers, as the administration's most recent "Attack on Media," continuing a pattern of hostility toward news organizations [4]. The lawsuit and the underlying report have ensured the Epstein case remains a central and damaging narrative for the administration.

**References:**
[1] Trump files $10 billion lawsuit over Wall Street Journal's Jeffrey Epstein report, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/trump-lawsuit-wall-street-journal-jeffrey-epstein-birthday-letter/

[2] Trump Sues Wall Street Journal Publisher Dow Jones Over Jeffrey Epstein Article, https://www.wsj.com/business/media/trump-sues-wall-street-journal-publisher-dow-jones-over-jeffrey-epstein-article-0257afee

[3] Trump on defensive over Epstein case following report he sent ‘bawdy’ letter, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/jul/18/trump-jeffrey-epstein-letter

[4] In Latest Attack on Media, Trump Sues Wall Street Journal Over Epstein Report, https://www.commondreams.org/news/trump-epstein

**1.2: Administration's Handling of Case Files and Investigations**
The administration's official strategy for managing the Epstein case files is drawing scrutiny. Attorney General Pam Bondi has formally requested the release of grand jury testimony related to the case as public pressure intensifies [1]. However, a more detailed report specifies the administration is selectively seeking the release of these grand jury records while simultaneously *not* requesting the release of the Justice Department's own internal files on its handling of the matter [2]. This nuanced approach has been accompanied by reports of internal friction, with President Trump said to be frustrated at having to "take the heat for Pam Bondi's handling of the Epstein files" [3]. On the matter of an independent probe, the White House, via spokesperson Leavitt, has stated the President "would not recommend" appointing a special prosecutor and is prepared to defer to the courts [4].

**References:**
[1] Pam Bondi asks to release Epstein grand jury testimony as Trump under fire, https://www.newsweek.com/jeffrey-epstein-files-doj-donald-trump-grand-jury-2101044

[2] Trump administration seeks release of Epstein grand jury records but not Justice Department files, https://apnews.com/article/trump-jeffrey-epstein-justice-department-bondi-91f911d2d7a909f78259cdca7b55d9a6

[3] Trump frustrated at having to take the heat for Pam Bondi's handling of the Epstein files, https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-administration/trump-frustrated-pam-bondi-handling-jeffrey-epstein-files-rcna219625

[4] Trump "would not recommend" appointing a special prosecutor in Epstein case, Leavitt says, https://www.cbsnews.com/colorado/news/trump-would-not-recommend-special-prosecutor-epstein-case-white-house-says/?intcid=CNR-01-0623

**1.3: Shifting Political Alliances and Cross-Party Dynamics**
The Epstein controversy is reshaping political alliances, most notably by creating a public fissure on the political right. President Trump's lawsuit against Rupert Murdoch's Wall Street Journal is being widely characterized as having ruptured a "critical bond that has shaped the US right" [1]. Another analysis questions why the Journal "isn't toeing the line," indicating a breakdown in the historically symbiotic relationship between the two figures [2]. Concurrently, the scandal is fostering unusual cross-party cooperation. An "unlikely alliance" between an unnamed Kentucky Republican and a California liberal has formed to jointly pressure the President for greater transparency and action on the Epstein case [3]. This pressure from both within and outside his party contributes to reports that the scandal is "haunting Trump's presidency" and sparking a "revolt" among his MAGA base [4].

**References:**
[1] Donald Trump’s lawsuit against Rupert Murdoch ruptures bond that has shaped the US right. The alliance has been beneficial to both men but has often been fractious, https://www.ft.com/content/9cbc70f4-bd31-4049-a5b1-9e670a48a5ec

[4] ‘The ghost of Epstein is haunting Trump’s presidency’: inside the ‘Maga’ revolt, https://www.theguardian.com/news/ng-interactive/2025/jul/19/trump-epstein-maga-revolt

**1.4: Victim Advocacy and Competing Public Narratives**
The public discourse is sharply divided between damning allegations and defiant support. Media outlets continue to scrutinize the President's past, with one report alleging he previously "worked to kill a story about his friendship with Epstein" and another framing the actions of his subordinates as an "Epstein Ponzi scheme" [1, 2]. A former model associated with Epstein has publicly claimed the two were once "best friends" who were "up to no good" [3]. Victim advocacy remains a potent element of the crisis. Survivors have stated that the administration's current handling of the case is adding to their "anguish," while one has publicly demanded the release of all files to "end impunity for rich & powerful abusers" [4, 5]. In direct opposition to this narrative, reports indicate that the President’s MAGA supporters are rallying around him specifically *because* of the Wall Street Journal article, with a sentiment of "We are so back" spreading online [6].

**Area 2: Executive Branch: Domestic Policy and Governance**

**2.1: Agency Restructuring and Budget Cuts**
The administration is implementing significant structural changes and budget reductions across federal agencies, impacting scientific and humanitarian functions. The Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) has officially shuttered its scientific research arm, a major move expected to impact hundreds of scientists [1]. This action mirrors events at the Department of Health and Human Services, where Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. is overseeing mass firings and budget cuts that have prompted health experts to raise alarms about a "war on science" [2]. Similar concerns have been voiced by the former leader of the State Department’s office for combating human trafficking, who reports the office is facing cuts that could undermine its mission [3].

**References:**
[1] EPA shutters its scientific research arm, with hundreds of scientists expected to be impacted, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/epa-shutters-its-scientific-research-arm-hundreds-of-scientists-expected-to-be-impacted/

[2] Health experts raise alarm over RFK Jr’s ‘war on science’ amid mass firings and budget cuts, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/jul/19/rfk-jr-science-research-cuts

[3] As State Department office combating human trafficking faces cuts, former leader weighs in, https://www.pbs.org/newshour/show/as-state-department-office-combating-human-trafficking-faces-cuts-former-leader-weighs-in

**2.2: Economic and Financial Regulation**
In a significant development for the financial technology sector, President Trump has signed new stablecoin regulations into law. The move is being hailed by proponents as a "major milestone for the crypto industry" and a key legislative accomplishment [1]. The President has also resumed his public criticism of Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell, stating that his refusal to lower interest rates is "costing the US a fortune." ## 3. Intelligence and Election Integrity

### 3.1. DNI Gabbard's Allegations on 2016 Election Intelligence
Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard has ignited a major political firestorm with the claim that Obama administration officials "manufactured intelligence" regarding Russian interference in the 2016 election [1]. According to DNI Gabbard, this was done to deliberately undermine Donald Trump's campaign [2]. The allegation has been met with a furious response from Democrats. Senator Mark Warner, a key figure on the Senate Intelligence Committee, publicly stated that DNI Gabbard is "not competent" for her role [3]. Republican lawmakers, however, have "erupted" in support of the claim, with one outlet reporting they see it as a "treasonous" plot that "makes Watergate look like amateur hour" [4]. This development is viewed by some commentators not as a genuine intelligence revelation, but as a calculated move to "feed MAGA an Obama conspiracy" and distract from the ongoing Epstein scandal [5].

[1] Gabbard claims Obama officials ‘manufactured intelligence’ of 2016 Russian election interference, https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/5409448-gabbard-alleges-obama-officials-manipulated-intelligence/  
[2] Gabbard Claims Obama Administration Tried to Undermine Trump in 2016, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/18/us/politics/gabbard-obama-trump-russia.html

### 3.2. State-Level Election Administration and Investigations
Concerns about election integrity are surfacing through incidents at the state level and ongoing federal investigations. A concerning report from Colorado details a consultant, who allegedly claimed to have White House backing, telephoning county clerks in an attempt to gain access to their voting machines [1]. In a separate case in Wisconsin, state elections officials have formally determined that a local clerk violated election laws in connection with an incident of uncounted ballots [2]. These state-level events are occurring as a House panel investigation into the previous administration continues; in the latest development, another former aide to President Biden has invoked their Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination during a deposition [3].

**References:**

## 4. Foreign Policy and International Relations

### 4.1. Diplomatic Actions in Latin America
A highly complex, multi-national prisoner exchange has been completed in Latin America. The deal involved Venezuela releasing jailed Americans, and in exchange, the U.S. arranged for El Salvador to free hundreds of U.S. deportees who were being held in a "notorious prison" [1] [2]. Following the exchange, "horror stories" are beginning to emerge from the Venezuelans who were released from the El Salvadoran facility, with some stating, "We were kidnapped" [3]. Separately, the U.S. is engaging in diplomatic pressure against Brazil. Secretary of State Marco Rubio announced the revocation of visas for several Brazilian judges, accusing them of carrying out a "political witch hunt" against former President Bolsonaro [4]. This action coincides with a prominent human rights group announcing its departure from El Salvador, citing direct threats from its government, further highlighting regional instability [5].

**References:**  
[1] Venezuela releases jailed Americans in deal that frees migrants deported to El Salvador by US, https://apnews.com/article/prisoner-swap-venezuela-united-states-el-salvador-a0c3070355fbdc31f028a16096c5655c  
[2] El Salvador releases hundreds of US deportees from notorious prison in US-Venezuela swap, https://amp.cnn.com/cnn/2025/07/18/politics/venezuela-us-prisoner-swap-trump  
[3] “We Were Kidnapped” — On Friday, more than 200 Venezuelans disappeared to a megaprison in El Salvador returned home. ### 4.2. U.S. Involvement in the Middle East and Trade Policy
The U.S. is facing new requests for involvement in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. An exclusive report from Axios states that Israel is actively seeking U.S. assistance to broker deals that would facilitate the movement of Palestinians out of the Gaza Strip [1]. Relations with the former U.S. administration are also a point of contention, as Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu has publicly accused the Biden administration of attempting to overthrow his government by funding protests and working to establish a left-wing government in Israel [2]. On the trade front, the Trump administration's policies continue to cause global economic disruption, with reports indicating the President's trade war is "upending China's factory floors" [3]. Beyond his public tariff pronouncements, the President is also said to be working on a "subtler tariff strategy," though the headlines provide no details on what this entails [4].

## 5. Media and Communications

### 5.1. The Cancellation of 'The Late Show with Stephen Colbert'
CBS has canceled "The Late Show with Stephen Colbert," a major disruption in the late-night television landscape that has elicited a direct response from the White House. President Trump celebrated the news, stating, "I Absolutely Love That Colbert Got Fired" [1]. CBS sources maintain the cancellation was a purely financial decision, citing "tens of millions in financial losses annually" and denying any political motivation [2]. However, the timing has raised widespread skepticism. Media critics note the "awful optics" of the decision [3], and multiple outlets are questioning if it was "really just a 'financial decision'" given the current political climate [4]. Public figure Rosie O’Donnell offered a sharper critique, labeling the move "blackmail" and accusing CBS of placating the President [5].

### 5.2. Funding for Public and Independent Media
The administration's budget cuts targeting public media are having a significant, negative impact, particularly on Native American communities. Leaders from Native American universities, colleges, and radio stations describe the cuts as "crippling" and "devastating" [1] [2]. They warn that the loss of funding directly threatens their ability to protect culture, provide public health information, and issue emergency alerts to their communities [3]. In the broader media ecosystem, one analysis suggests that the conservative media platform PragerU is strategically "primed to capitalize" on the funding void created by the administration's cuts to PBS, potentially altering the public media landscape [4].

## 6. Other Key Legal and Political Items

### 6.1. Federal Judiciary Developments
Two federal court developments are noteworthy. First, a judge has dismissed President Trump's lawsuit against journalist Bob Woodward, which centered on an audiobook compilation of their interviews [1]. Second, a federal appeals court judge has made the assertion that the First Amendment's protections do not apply to non-citizens. This claim is described in one report as being made "against all historical evidence," suggesting it represents a significant and controversial departure from established legal precedent [2].

**References:**

### 6.2. State-Level Legal Rulings and Political Interests
At the state level, a judge in Washington has blocked a state law that would have required priests to report instances of child abuse disclosed during a confession, a ruling with significant implications for mandatory reporting laws [1]. In Minnesota, a state lawmaker has been convicted of felony burglary for illegally entering the home of his estranged stepmother [2]. Separately, President Trump has publicly stated his desire for the Texas GOP to use the state's redistricting process to pick up an additional five House seats, indicating a direct presidential interest in state-level apportionment [3].
